## 6. AI Simulation Scenario Ideas

### Scenario 1 — "The Technical Domain Mock Assessment"
**Homeowner type:** Engineer, analytical, asks probing follow-up questions
**Setup:** Full 15-minute simulated appointment segment covering solar physics (how it works), inverter type recommendation, and battery backup capability. The homeowner pushes back on every answer: "Why?" "Are you sure?" "My neighbor's rep told me something different."
**Skill being tested:** Demonstrating accurate V2 technical knowledge under pressure from a skeptical homeowner — without over-claiming, without becoming defensive, and without retreating to vague or outdated language.
**Pass criteria:** Rep explains the solar chain accurately, handles the inverter question without blanket-recommending a type, handles the battery backup question with accurate configuration language, maintains composure throughout, and does not make any claim that would fail the self-audit rubric.

---

### Scenario 2 — "The Financial Domain Mock Assessment"
**Homeowner type:** Financially savvy, did research, has a specific question about TOU rates and the tax credit
**Setup:** Homeowner says: "I'm on a TOU plan with SCE. I've been reading about how solar interacts with TOU rates and I'm confused about when my panels produce vs. when I pay peak rates. Also — what exactly is the current federal tax credit situation? I've heard it's changed."
**Skill being tested:** Demonstrating accurate V2 financial knowledge on TOU rate structure and the current incentive landscape — using verification-first language and honest production timing explanation without defaulting to oversimplified or outdated answers.
**Pass criteria:** Rep accurately explains the TOU production timing mismatch (midday production vs. evening peak rates), correctly positions battery as the financial solution, uses verification-first language on the tax credit question, and does not quote a specific credit percentage without appropriate caveats.

---

### Scenario 3 — "The Full Domain Assessment Simulation"
**Homeowner type:** Composite — a challenging but fair homeowner who tests across all five domains in one conversation
**Setup:** A 20-minute assessment simulation covering: how solar works (technical), how TOU rates affect savings (financial), whether a battery makes sense for their TOU market (battery/NEM), what the rep noticed about the roof and panel during their visit (site awareness), and what happens after they sign (post-sale operations).
**Skill being tested:** Demonstrating V2 competency across all five domains in a realistic conversation flow — the closest simulation to the Day 7 assessment.
**Pass criteria:** Rep covers all five domains accurately, uses compliant language throughout, does not over-claim on any topic, handles follow-up questions with composure, and demonstrates the ability to guide the conversation naturally between topics rather than delivering five separate monologues.

---

## 7. Quiz / Assessment Ideas

**1. Multiple Choice**
The Day 7 Technical Authority assessment is evaluating:
- A) Whether reps can recite V2 module content from memory
- B) Whether reps can apply V2 knowledge accurately and confidently in realistic scenario-based conversations
- C) Whether reps have completed all V2 workbook exercises
- D) Whether reps can correctly identify the five V2 knowledge domains
*(Correct answer: B)*

**2. Short Answer**
A rep scores themselves 0 in the Battery & NEM domain on the self-assessment. What should their preparation plan look like for the 48 hours before the Day 7 assessment?

**3. Multiple Choice**
In a Day 7 assessment scenario, a rep is asked how a battery adds value for a homeowner on a TOU plan. The best answer is:
- A) "Batteries protect you from outages — that's their main value."
- B) "A battery stores the power your panels produce at midday and lets you use it during the evening peak rate window instead of buying from the grid at peak rates — that's where the real financial value is in a TOU market."
- C) "Batteries are expensive but worth it for the peace of mind."
- D) "You should ask your installer about which battery is best for your system."
*(Correct answer: B)*

**4. Scenario Judgment**
During the Day 7 assessment role-play, a rep tells the homeowner: "Your payback period is exactly 9.4 years." What flag should the assessor note — and what corrected version would pass?
*(Expected answer: The assessor should flag "precision without qualification" — payback period calculations depend on multiple variables including future utility rates. The corrected version: "Based on your current bill, the system design, and the financing terms we're looking at, the estimated payback period is in the 9–11 year range. If utility rates continue the trend we've seen in this area, it could be shorter.")*

**5. Fill in the Blank**
The five V2 knowledge domains are: _______ Technical Foundation, _______ Fluency, Battery & _______, Discovery & Site _______, and Post-Sale _______.
*(Correct: Solar; Financial; NEM; Awareness; Operations)*

## 9. Trainer Script Outline

**Opener (2–3 min)**
"We've covered a lot over the last six days. Solar physics, inverters, batteries, TOU rates, incentive compliance, financing structures, discovery questions, survey prep, escalation paths, save-the-deal communication, referrals, CRM discipline, and self-coaching. That's the V2 curriculum. Tomorrow, you're going to prove that it's not just something you heard — it's something you can do. And today, we're going to make sure you walk in tomorrow as prepared as possible."

**Concept Explanation (10 min)**
Walk through the five domains and the self-assessment framework. Give reps 5 minutes to complete the self-assessment honestly. Ask for 2–3 volunteers to share which domain they scored lowest — normalize the honesty.

**Example (5 min)**
"Here's what the difference looks like between a rep who's prepared and one who isn't. Question: 'What's the current federal tax credit for solar?' Unprepared rep: 'It's 30% — you'll get a third of your system cost back.' Prepared rep: 'There are significant federal incentive programs currently available — how much you benefit from the tax credit specifically depends on your individual tax situation, and your accountant would be the right person to confirm that for your scenario. What I can tell you is it's been one of the most meaningful incentives in the market.' Which rep are you walking into Day 7 as? Let's make sure it's the second one."

**Activity Transition (10 min)**
Exercise 6.4A-2 (Practice Question Sprint) — reps choose 5 questions from their weakest domains and answer them verbally to a partner. This is the most important preparation activity in the session. Give full time to it.

**Wrap-Up (3 min)**
"Tomorrow isn't a test of whether you're smart. It's a test of whether you're prepared. The preparation you do tonight — the practice questions you answer out loud, the domains you review, the improvement commitments you carry forward — that's what tomorrow looks like. You've done the work. Now do the preparation. See you on the other side."

#### CONTENT SECTIONS
**The Reputation Compound Effect**  
Every interaction you have either builds or erodes your reputation. Every honest conversation is a deposit. Every exaggeration is a withdrawal. Reps who think short-term chase any deal, overpromise, and burn bridges. Reps who think long-term qualify aggressively, build relationships, and generate referrals for years. Twenty-five closed deals means twenty-five potential referral sources. One hundred closed deals means enough inbound business to rarely cold knock. Treat every customer like a five-year relationship \u2014 because the best ones become exactly that.

### Module 6.5: Advanced Scenario Practice
- **ID:** mod_6_5
- **Subtitle:** Integrate all skills in complex, real-world simulations Practice under pressure Receive detailed feedback
#### CONTENT SECTIONS
**Scenario A \u2014 The Researcher**  
This homeowner has researched NEM 3.0, dealer fees, and degradation curves before you arrived. They're testing your expertise. Don't repeat basics \u2014 ask what they've already learned and where their gaps are. Use technical language. Admit when you need to confirm exact figures rather than bluffing. Then ask: based on everything you've researched, what's the one thing still holding you back? That question almost always surfaces the real blocker \u2014 which is usually not technical at all.

**Scenario B \u2014 Married Couple Standoff**  
Husband wants solar. Wife is skeptical from a prior contractor experience. And there's a hidden issue \u2014 they're planning to sell in four years. Your job is to balance enthusiasm for the husband with trust-building for the wife, address the four-year timeline honestly \u2014 which may mean a partial disqualification or an honest conversation about shorter payback structures \u2014 and never take sides. Validate both perspectives. Make the wife feel heard before she feels sold. Her trust is the key to the deal.

**Scenario C \u2014 Competing Quote**  
A warm referral lead \u2014 already motivated and mostly educated. But they got a competing quote eight thousand dollars cheaper. Your response is never to panic or drop your price reflexively. Walk them through the right comparison questions: what panels, what inverter, what warranty, who does the install, what's the monitoring system, and what's the cancellation policy? Eight thousand dollars in savings means nothing if the cheaper company uses inferior components, subcontracts the install, or doesn't exist in five years when a warranty claim comes in. Make the case for value, not price.

#### SLIDE DECK OUTLINE
*No specific slides defined for this module.*
#### WORKBOOK PROMPTS
- Reflect on Advanced Scenario Practice: How will you apply this?
#### QUIZ DATA

### Module 6.6: Certification Exam
- **ID:** mod_6_6
- **Subtitle:** missing_from_source
#### CONTENT SECTIONS
**Exam Overview**  
The certification exam is fifty questions covering five areas. Solar technology and system components \u2014 twenty percent. Utility bill analysis and financing \u2014 twenty percent. Homeowner psychology and the BOLT framework \u2014 twenty percent. Objection handling and closing \u2014 twenty-five percent. Compliance and ethics \u2014 fifteen percent. You need an eighty percent or higher to pass. This isn't a test you pass by studying hard the night before \u2014 it's a test you pass by being fully present through Days One through Six. If you've done the work, you're ready.

After lunch, you run one full appointment yourself, with your manager observing quietly. Then you debrief, receive your field assessment, and get cleared for solo selling. Get a good night's sleep. You are ready.

## DAY 7: Field Certification & Launch
### Module 7.1: Pre-Field Briefing
- **ID:** mod_7_1
- **Subtitle:** Review Day 7 agenda Set expectations for shadowing Address any last-minute questions
#### CONTENT SECTIONS
**Shadow Mode \u2014 What to Watch For**  
This morning you are in shadow mode. Your job is to observe and take notes \u2014 not to participate unless your manager invites you to. As you watch each appointment, focus on five things: how your manager positions themselves physically in the home, how they handle unexpected interruptions, how they identify and adapt to personality types in real time, how they phrase objection responses differently from how they were scripted, and when and how they make the close. After each appointment, you'll debrief in the car. Ask every question that came up.

### Module 7.2: Appointment #1 \u2014 Shadow & Observe
- **ID:** mod_7_2
- **Subtitle:** missing_from_source
#### CONTENT SECTIONS
**Debrief After Appointment 1**  
After each shadow appointment, the debrief in the car is as important as the appointment itself. Your manager will ask what you noticed. Bring specific observations \u2014 not general thoughts. Then your manager will walk you through what they were thinking at key moments. Why they slowed down when the wife got quiet. Why they chose the summary close instead of the assumptive close. Why they asked about the electric vehicle at that specific point in the discovery. These context moments turn observation into insight.

### Module 7.3: Appointment #2 \u2014 Shadow & Observe
- **ID:** mod_7_3
- **Subtitle:** missing_from_source
#### CONTENT SECTIONS
**Constructive Critique**  
After the second appointment, your manager will ask: what would you have done differently? This is not a test \u2014 it's a reflection exercise. Think about moments where the conversation could have gone another direction. When did the homeowner give a buying signal that wasn't immediately recognized? What objection could have been handled with a different technique? This kind of constructive critique \u2014 whether on your manager's appointment or your own \u2014 is how elite reps develop faster than average ones.

What discovery questions will you lead with? What personality type do you expect based on the lead info? What objections might come up? How do you plan to close? Articulating this out loud is a form of mental rehearsal that significantly improves execution. Your manager will coach any adjustments before you go in.

### Module 7.5: Pre-Appointment Prep
- **ID:** mod_7_5
- **Subtitle:** missing_from_source
#### CONTENT SECTIONS
**Last-Minute Coaching**  
In the fifteen minutes before your appointment, your manager will ask you five questions. What do you know about this homeowner? What's your opener? What objections do you expect? Which homeowner type does this feel like? And how will you close? Answer all five out loud. Don't guess \u2014 draw on your training. Then take a breath. You've practiced this for six days. You know the framework. You know the objections. You know how to read a room. Trust your preparation and go execute.

### Module 7.6: Rep Runs Full Appointment
- **ID:** mod_7_6
- **Subtitle:** missing_from_source
#### CONTENT SECTIONS
**Running the Appointment**  
This is your moment. Your manager will sit quietly and observe \u2014 they will not intervene unless you freeze or the homeowner asks them a direct question. Your job is to run the full appointment from discovery through close as if no one else is in the room. Use everything from Day One through Six. Control the environment. Read the personality. Ask all twelve discovery questions. Deliver the value stack. Handle every objection with A.C.A. Ask for the sale. And if they close \u2014 ask for a referral before you leave. This is real. Do your job.

### Module 7.7: Post-Appointment Debrief
- **ID:** mod_7_7
- **Subtitle:** missing_from_source
#### CONTENT SECTIONS
**Manager Feedback Framework**  
Your manager will debrief using a three-part structure. First, what went well \u2014 specific things you did well, with examples from the appointment. Second, what to improve \u2014 one or two specific, actionable adjustments for your next appointment. Third, your overall assessment: field-ready means you start setting appointments immediately. Almost there means one more shadowing day. Needs more training means continued role-play before solo selling. Regardless of the outcome \u2014 you ran a real appointment today. That puts you ahead of where you started seven days ago.

You are now an active solar consultant. The certificate is not the end \u2014 it's the beginning. Every appointment from here builds your skill, your pipeline, and your reputation. Go earn it.
